The **Defensive-qi** moves contrary, the **Nourishing-qi** moves with—if one knows this, one may adjust it.
The method of **调** (*adjusting*) **qi** must lie in **yin-yang**.
The methods of **调摄** (*adjusting and nurturing*) **Nourishing** and **Defensive** **qi** lie in **yin-yang** and **虚实** (*void/full*).
What does this mean?
How does this principle work?"

Now then, what is meant by *welcoming* and *following* is knowing the circulation of **Nourishing** and **Defensive** **qi**, and the passage of vessels and collaterals.

Only by knowing the circulation of **Nourishing** and **Defensive** **qi** and the passage of vessels and collaterals can one avoid failing to supplement, drain, welcome, or follow. Following their contrary or with movements to take **qi**, hence the terms *welcoming* and *following*.

Since the **Defensive-qi** moves contrary and the **Nourishing-qi** moves with, one supplements or drains according to their contrary or with movements—thus *welcoming* and *following*.

The method of **adjusting qi** must lie in **yin-yang**, for:

When **yin** is void and **yang** is full, one supplements **yin** and drains **yang**;
When **yang** is void and **yin** is full, one supplements **yang** and drains **yin**.

Sometimes **yang** dominates **yin**, sometimes **yin** dominates **yang**;
Sometimes both **yin** and **yang** are void, sometimes both are full.
In all cases, one adjusts **yin-yang** according to where the disease lies, and thus no disease remains unresolved.

Knowing the inner and outer, the superficial and deep:
Observing the collaterals’ floating state, discerning the disease’s void or fullness—
Using the inner to know the outer, the outer to know the inner,
Viewing the superficial to know the deep, the deep to know the superficial—
Thus one knows void and fullness.

Adjusting according to **yin-yang**, treating each according to which **yin-yang** vessel the disease resides in—
Hence it is said: *The method of adjusting qi must lie in yin-yang.*

Reiterating the previous text,
The **73rd Difficulty** says:

The **Ping** points—where the flesh is thin and the **qi** insufficient to command—how must one treat them?
The **Ping** points are located at the fingertips of hands and feet, where the flesh is thin and the **blood-qi** is still scant; how then may one apply needle insertion?

Yet it is said:
The **Ping** points belong to **Wood**;
The **Rong** points belong to **Fire**.
**Ping** is the mother of **Fire**;
**Rong** is the child of **Wood**.
**Fire**, being the child of **Wood’s child**, when treating the **Ping** points,
must be drained by the **Rong** points.
If the **Liver (Wood)** is full, fullness must be drained from its child.
The **Rong** points belong to **Fire**, the child of **Wood**,
so they must be drained.
In spring, one needles the **Rong**—this is the **Emperor (Wood)** not yet concluding its reign,
as **Fire** seizes the **Emperor’s** rule—
a principle of **real evil**, hence the draining of **Rong**.

For instance, if the **Liver** itself is diseased,
when full, one drains the **Fire** within the **Liver**,
when void, one supplements the **Wood** within the **Liver**.
Thus the Classics say: *"The method of supplementing cannot be used for draining, nor can draining be used for supplementing."*
When one should supplement, draining is forbidden;
when one should drain, supplementing is forbidden.

The **74th Difficulty** asks:
The Classics say: *"In spring, needle the **Ping** points."*
**Ping** belongs to **Wood**, so in spring it is needled.
In summer, needle the **Rong** points.
**Rong** belongs to **Fire**, so in summer it is needled.
In late summer, needle the **Yu** points.
**Yu** belongs to **Earth**, so in late summer—June—it is needled.
In autumn, needle the **Jing** points.
**Jing** belongs to **Metal**, so in autumn it is needled.
In winter, needle the **He** points.
**He** belongs to **Water**, so in winter it is needled.

What does this mean?
How do the needleings differ in the four seasons?

Yet it is said:
In spring, when needling the **Ping** points, the **evil** is in the **Liver**.
To prevent **Liver (Wood)** evil from harming **Spleen (Earth)**, one needles the **Ping** points.
In summer, when needling the **Rong** points, the **evil** is in the **Heart**.
To prevent **Heart (Fire)** evil from harming **Lung (Metal)**, one needles the **Rong** points.
In late summer, when needling the **Yu** points, the **evil** is in the **Spleen**.
To prevent **Spleen (Earth)** evil from harming **Kidney (Water)**, one needles the **Yu** points.
In autumn, when needling the **Jing** points, the **evil** is in the **Lung**.
To prevent **Lung (Metal)** evil from harming **Liver (Wood)**, one needles the **Jing** points.
In winter, when needling the **He** points, the **evil** is in the **Kidney**.
To prevent **Kidney (Water)** evil from harming **Heart (Fire)**, one needles the **He** points.

Why does the **Liver, Heart, Spleen, Lung, Kidney** system relate to the four seasons?
How are the five **Zang** organs connected to the four seasons?

Yet it is said:
When one **Zang** organ is diseased, the five **evils** manifest.
The five **tones**, five **colors**, five **flavors**, five **fragrances**, and five **bodily fluids**.
For instance, if the **Liver** is diseased—
taking the **Liver** as a single organ for example—
greenish **color** belongs to the **Liver**,
a **sour odor** belongs to the **Liver**,
a preference for **sour tastes** belongs to the **Liver**,
a tendency to **laugh** belongs to the **Liver**,
and a tendency to **weep** belongs to the **Liver**.
*(See annotation in the **34th Difficulty**.)*
Its diseases are manifold—
too numerous to exhaustively enumerate.

「Diseases are most numerous—though spoken of, they cannot be fully exhausted.
The four seasons have their own fixed **numbers**, yet they all converge upon **Spring, Summer, Autumn, Winter** as well.

The four seasons have a definite **cycle**, all linked to this.
The essential subtlety of **needling** lies in its **autumn-hair** precision—this is the key.
The **autumn-hair** principle refers to the acupuncture’s delicate and refined logic.

The **75th Difficulty** states:
The **Canon** says, *"The East is solid, the West is void; drain the South, supplement the North—what does this mean?"*
If the **Liver** (East) is **solid**, and the **Lung** (West) is **void**,
then drain the **Heart-Fire** (South) and supplement the **Kidney-Water** (North)—how so?

Yet: **Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, Earth** must balance one another.
**Metal** overcomes **Wood**, **Wood** overcomes **Earth**, **Earth** overcomes **Water**, **Water** overcomes **Fire**, **Fire** overcomes **Metal**—
the five **Zang** organs and the five **Phases** must mutually regulate and subdue one another.
One should rely on their **supplementation and drainage** to harmonize and treat accordingly.

The East belongs to **Wood**.
The East is governed by **Wood**.
The West belongs to **Metal**.
The West is governed by **Metal**.
When **Wood** seeks to be **solid**, **Metal** must balance it.
If **Metal** overcomes **Wood**, then **Liver-qi** grows **strong and solid**, while **Lung-qi** becomes **weak and void**—
**Wood** rebels against **Metal**, and **Metal**’s family does not submit,
so **Metal** comes to balance **Wood**.

When **Fire** seeks to be **solid**, **Water** must balance it.
If **Heart-qi** grows **strong and solid**, while **Kidney-qi** becomes **weak and void**—
**Fire** rebels against **Water**, and **Water**’s family does not submit,
so **Water** comes to balance **Fire**.

When **Earth** seeks to be **solid**, **Wood** must balance it.
If **Spleen-qi** grows **strong and solid**, while **Liver-qi** becomes **weak and void**—
**Earth** rebels against **Wood**, and **Wood**’s family does not submit,
so **Wood** comes to balance **Earth**.

When **Metal** seeks to be **solid**, **Fire** must balance it.
If **Lung-qi** grows **strong and solid**, while **Heart-qi** becomes **weak and void**—
**Metal** rebels against **Fire**, and **Fire**’s family does not submit,
so **Fire** comes to balance **Metal**.

When **Water** seeks to be **solid**, **Earth** must balance it.
If **Kidney-qi** grows **strong and solid**, while **Spleen-qi** becomes **weak and void**—
**Earth** rebels against **Water**, and **Water**’s family does not submit,
so **Earth** comes to balance **Water**.

If the East is the **Liver**, then one knows the **Liver** is **solid**;
if the West is the **Lung**, then one knows the **Lung** is **void**.
When **pathogenic-qi** flourishes, it becomes **solid**;
when **true-qi** is depleted, it becomes **void**.
**Wood** being **solid** means **Wood** has excess—
then **Earth** grows **rampant and fearful**, and **Metal** lacks nourishment,
leading to **Metal**’s **voidness**.

To drain the **Heart-Fire** (South) and supplement the **Kidney-Water** (North):
The **Heart-Fire** (South) is the **child** of **Wood**.
The **Kidney-Water** (North) is the **mother** of **Wood**.
**Water** overcomes **Fire**.

Taking the **Liver** as a single organ for example:
**Fire** is the **child** of **Wood**.
If one does not drain **Fire**, then **Fire** will flourish excessively and **consumptively** attack **Metal**,
**Metal** will retaliate and **overwhelm** **Wood**,
and **Metal** and **Wood** will mutually **assail** one another.

**Water** is the **mother** of **Wood**.
If one does not supplement **Water**, then **Water-qi** will be **weak**,
and it will fail to generate **Wood**.
The **child** can cause the **mother** to be **solid**,
and the **mother** can cause the **child** to be **void**.
The **child** can make the **mother** **excessively solid**,
and the **mother** can make the **child** **weakly void**.

Thus, draining **Fire** and supplementing **Water**,
one seeks to prevent **Metal** from balancing **Wood**.
In applying **needling** to drain,
one must first diagnose its **manifestations**—
then drain the **Heart**, so that **Heart-qi** flows freely,
and **Liver-qi** is restored.
Then supplement the **Kidney**, so that **Kidney**’s family receives **qi**,
and **Kidney** transmits **qi** to nourish the **Liver**.
Once **Liver-qi** is **settled**, then **Lung** will no longer come to balance the **Liver**.

As the **Canon** states:
*"If one cannot treat its **voidness**, why ask about its excess?"*
This is the very meaning.

If **Lung-voidness** arises from **Liver-solidity**, then one must drain **Fire** and supplement **Water**.
If one does not grasp the essential principle of treating **voidness**,
why bother inquire about the rest?

The **76th Difficulty** asks:
*"What is meant by **supplementation and drainage**?"*

The meaning of **supplementation** and **drainage**—how so?

When one must **supplement**, from where does one draw **qi**?
When the time comes to **supplement**, from where does one take **qi**?

When one must **drain**, where does one place **qi**?
**Placement** is **taking**, is **welcoming**.
When the time comes to **drain**, from where does one take **qi**?

Now: when **supplementing**, one takes **qi** from the **Wei** [defensive circulation].
The **Lung** governs the five **qi**, irrigating and nourishing the five **zàng** [solid organs],
circulating through the six **jīng** [channels], and returning to the hundred **tún** [pores].
To take **qi**, one must draw it from the **Wei**—
once **qi** is obtained, one then inserts the needle into the **zàng** or **fu** [hollow organ] channels where **voidness** resides,
adjusting depth and section accordingly—this is how one **supplements**.

When **draining**, one places **qi** in the **Rong** [nutritive circulation].
Since **pathogens** dwell in the **Rong**, one inserts the needle into the **zàng** or **fu** channels where **solidity** resides,
waiting for the **qi** to guide the needle as it **drains**.

If **yang-qi** is insufficient and **yin-qi** is in excess,
one must first **supplement the yang**, then **drain the yin**.
For instance, if the **Gallbladder** is deficient and the **Liver** is in excess,
one first **supplements the Foot-Shao-Yang** [Gallbladder channel], then **drains the Foot-Jué-Yin** [Liver channel].

If **yin-qi** is insufficient and **yang-qi** is in excess,
one must first **supplement the yin**, then **drain the yang**.
If the **Liver** is deficient and the **Gallbladder** is in excess,
one first **supplements the Foot-Jué-Yin** [Liver channel], then **drains the Foot-Shao-Yang** [Gallbladder channel].

The **Rong** and **Wei** circulate harmoniously—this is the key principle.
When **yin** or **yang** is in excess or deficiency,
one must first **supplement what is deficient**, then **drain what is in excess**—
thus ensuring the **Rong** and **Wei** flow freely, which is the very essence of needle technique.

The **77th Difficulty** asks:
*"The **Canon** says: 'The superior physician treats disease before it arises.'"*

The **superior physician**—the master healer who ensures complete success in every case—is one who treats illness before it manifests. The **mediocre physician** treats only when disease has already arisen. The mediocre physician fails to grasp the full principle, and thus remains fixed on treating a single organ alone.

What does this mean? How is this explained?

When it is said to treat illness before it arises, it means: when one observes disease in the **Liver**, one knows the **Liver** will transmit it to the **Spleen**, so one must first **fortify the Spleen’s qi**, preventing it from receiving the **Liver’s** pathogenic influence. Among the five **zàng** organs, those in excess transmit their imbalance, while those deficient receive evil. When observing disease in the **Liver** channel, one recognizes that the **Spleen**—the organ it overcomes—will be affected, so one preemptively **supplements the Spleen’s qi**, preventing it from receiving the **Liver’s** pathogenic *qi*. Thus, it is said to treat illness before it arises.

Returning to the previous text:

The **mediocre physician**, upon seeing disease in the **Liver**, does not understand the principle of transmission, and thus focuses solely on treating the **Liver**. Seeing disease in the **Liver**, they fail to grasp the logic of the **Liver** transmitting to the **Spleen**, and instead concentrate only on treating the **Liver** channel. Hence, it is said they treat illness only after it has arisen.

Returning to the previous text.

---

**Chapter 78: On the Difficulties of Needling**

Needling has methods of **supplementation** and **drainage**. In **supplementation**, one exhales as the needle is withdrawn; in **drainage**, one inhales as the needle is inserted. What does this mean? How are these methods explained?

Indeed: the methods of **supplementation** and **drainage** do not strictly require exhaling or inhaling to withdraw or insert the needle. The true methods of **supplementation** and **drainage** are not concealed in the breath’s withdrawal or insertion, but rather rely on the **arrival of *qi*** as the needle enters or exits.

For those who know needling: they trust their **left hand**. When applying needling techniques, they begin with the **left hand**. For those who do not know needling: they trust their **right hand**. When ignorant of needling methods, they begin with the **right hand**. At the moment of insertion:

Before needling, one must first press and stabilize the **acupuncture point** with the **left hand**. Knowing the location of the **acupuncture point**, one presses it firmly with the **left hand**. Then, one **flicks and strains** it—with the **right hand**, one flicks the pressed point, causing the **skin’s *qi*** to swell beneath. One **hooks and lowers** the needle—**hooks and lowers** it, aligning the needle’s position. When the *qi* arrives, it appears like the **pulsing of a vein**. The *qi* arrives beneath the **left hand’s** pressure, manifesting like the **pulsing of skin** (*fǔ*). Following this, one needles along the needle’s path. Upon **arrival of *qi***, one then **pushes and inserts** the needle deeper into the **meridian**. This is called **supplementation**.

If one **flicks and lifts** it, this is called **drainage**. When *qi* arrives, one **shakes and withdraws** the needle, and this is **drainage**. If *qi* does not arrive:

If the needle is left in place for a long time and *qi* still does not come, one waits in the **Wei** layer for the *qi* to arrive; if it still does not come, one inserts deeper into the **meridian** (*Hóng*) and waits again. If, after probing these three levels—**Wei**, **meridian**, and **meridian** (*Hóng*)—the *qi* fails to respond beneath the needle, this signifies that the **Yin and Yang** have both been exhausted, and further needling is impossible. This is the case of **"male external, female internal"**—if *qi* does not arrive, it is called **"ten deaths, one survival"**.

The **Wei** layer governs **Yang**, overseeing the **external**; in males, **Yang *qi*** circulates externally, so one uses a **light touch** to press the point. The **meridian** (*Hóng*) governs **blood**, overseeing the **internal**; in females, **Yin *qi*** circulates internally, so one uses a **heavy touch** to press the point. If *qi* does not arrive even after the proper timing, and the **left hand** fails to sense it, then needling is impossible, resulting in **"ten deaths, one survival"**.

---

**Chapter 79: On the Difficulties of Needling**

The **classics** state: *"迎而夺之"*—how can this not result in **emptiness**? When the *qi* is just about to arrive and one uses the needle to take it, this is called *"迎而夺之"*. **迎 (Yíng)** means to **take the *qi***; **夺 (Duó)** means to **drain the *qi***. How can taking and draining it not result in **emptiness**?

The **classics** also state: *"随而济之"*—how can this not result in **fullness**? **随 (Suí)** means to **follow the *qi*** from the **Wei** layer and **supplement** it. **济 (Jì)** means to **reinforce the deficient meridian**. How can following and reinforcing it not result in **fullness**? When the *qi* flows and settles, one inserts the needle; once the needle is withdrawn, one **palpates the point**—this is called *"随而济之"*.

**Emptiness** and **fullness** are matters of **arrival or failure**. If the meridian is **weak**, yet one needles to **supplement its fullness**, the result is either **arrival or failure**—this is the critical point. If the meridian is **strong**, yet one needles to **drain its emptiness**, the result is either **arrival or failure**—this is also the critical point.

What does this mean? How are these methods explained?

Thus:

When **welcoming and taking**—this is **draining its child**. If the five **zàng** are **full**, drain their child. When **following and supplementing**—this is **reinforcing its mother**. If the five **zàng** are **empty**, supplement their mother.

Take, for instance, a **heart** disease. Using the **heart** as an example for one **zàng**:
Drain the **Shou Xin Zhu** (Palace) point. The **heart** is the sovereign of the five **zàng**; by law, it does not receive disease. What receives disease is the **heart’s pericardium**. The **Shou Xin Zhu** is the **hand Jueyin Heart-Pericardium** meridian’s **shu** point. The **Shou Xin Zhu** point is **earth**; the **heart’s fire** is its child—thus, draining its **shu** point is draining its child. This is **welcoming and taking**.

Referring back to the previous text: Supplement the **Shou Xin Zhu** **jing** (well) point. The **heart’s fire** is the child of **wood**; **wood** is the **mother** of **fire**. Now, supplementing the **well** of the **Shou Xin Zhu** is supplementing its mother. This is called **following and supplementing**.

What is meant by **fullness** and **emptiness**? This refers to **tao (牢)** and **ru (濡)**.
**Ru** is **emptiness**; **tao** is **fullness**.
When *qi* arrives **tao** and **full**, it is **success**; when **ru** and **empty**, it is **failure**—thus, *"either success or failure."*

Before performing **supplementation or drainage**, first **palpate** the **zàng**’s **shu** points and the points to be needled. If the *qi* arrives **tao** and **full**, it may be drained; if **ru** and **empty**, it may be supplemented. If one holds the needle and cannot **discern** its **tao** or **ru**, then it is *"either success or failure."*

The *Ba Shi Nan* (Eighty Difficulties) asks:
The classics say: *"There are those who see [the needle] as entering, those who see the needle as entering, and those who see [the needle] as exiting."* What does this mean? How is *"seeing the needle as exiting"*?

Thus:
What is meant by *"seeing as entering"* is that the left hand **observes** the *qi* arriving before inserting the needle. When needling a person, first use the left hand to **palpate** the *qi* in the **an** (安) region. When the *qi* arrives, then insert the needle. The needle enters the point. When the *qi* is exhausted, withdraw the needle. **Palpate** until the *qi* is exhausted before withdrawing the needle—this is not the method of **welcoming, following, supplementation, or drainage**. This is called *"seeing as entering, seeing as exiting."*

Summarizing the previous text.

The **Eighty-One Difficulties** states: *"The Classics speak of ‘solid-solid, hollow-hollow’ [needling], and of ‘draining the deficient while supplementing the excessive.’"* Refer to the annotations on the **Twelfth Difficulty**.

Is this regarding the *cùnkǒu* (寸口) pulse? Ask: *"What is the pulse like?"* Is this regarding the patient’s inherent deficiency or excess? Ask: *"Does the disease itself have deficiency or excess?"*

How does one apply the method of **draining** and **supplementing**?

Suppose the **liver** is solid (real) while the **lungs** are hollow (deficient). The liver is **wood**, the lungs are **metal**. Metal and wood should **mutually balance**—metal should **subdue** wood. See the **Seventy-Fifth Difficulty** for details.

Suppose the lungs are solid. For instance, if the **lung-qi** is strong and excessive, one would recognize that the liver is deficient with **scant and faint** *qi*.

If the liver’s *qi* is **weak and deficient**, **fine and sparse**, yet the practitioner **needles without supplementing the liver** and instead **further strengthens the lungs**, this is the error of **draining the deficient while supplementing the excessive**.

Thus, the saying *"solid-solid, hollow-hollow"* and *"draining the deficient while supplementing the excessive"* is the **harm** caused by **mediocre practitioners**.

This is the **harm** of mediocre practitioners, whereby they apply *"solid-solid, hollow-hollow"* and *"drain the deficient while supplementing the excessive."*

---

**Annotations for reference:**
#61: *内* (nèi) – "insert"
#62: *时* (shí) – "when"
#63: *安* (ān) – "an" (安穴, a pulse region)
#64: *经言* (jīng yán) – "The Classics say"
#65: *损不足而益有余* (sǔn bùzú ér yì yǒuyú) – "drain the deficient while supplementing the excessive" (a TCM acupuncture principle)
#66: *假* (jiǎ) – "Suppose"

「#59 *Xū* [虚]: According to the original text, this should likely be *"shí"* [实].
#60 *Hú* [胡]: In *Jízhù* [集注], the seventy-ninth *nàn* [难] (Ding) [丁] reads *"míng"* [明].
#61 *Nèi* [内]: Below this, *Běnyì* [本义] includes the character *"zhēn"* [针].
#62 *Rén shí* [人时]: In *Jízhù* [集注], the eighty-ninth *nàn* [难] (Ding) [丁] reads *"rén mài"* [人脉].
#63 *Ān* [安]: In *Jízhù* [集注], the eighty-ninth *nàn* [难] (Ding) [丁] reads *"xué"* [穴].
#64 *Yán* [言]: Below this, *Jízhù* [集注] includes the character *"wú"* [无].
#65 *Yú* [余]: Originally omitted, restored from *Běnyì* [本义].
#66 *Jiǎ* [假]: Before this, *Běnyì* [本义] has the following sixteen characters: 『然是病非谓寸口脉也，谓病自有虚实也』.」
